In addition, the findings for the interviews align with the survey's findings. As one of the
IT managers (P13) remarked, technical values and beliefs stemmed from experience. In
view of this, employees needed to be educated about technological innovations such as
the Cloud, so that they could incorporate an understanding of its functions into whatever
pre-existing technology culture they possessed. This was what had happened in his retail
SMEs, and it had facilitated the acceptance of cloud computing technology.

The quantitative and qualitative findings highlighted that Saudi SMEs' technology culture
does not affect their intention to adopt cloud computing, which resulted in the rejection
of the hypothesis (H15).

7.1.16 Awareness
The survey findings support the hypothesis (H16): Increasing the awareness of IT
managers, top managers, and employees increases Saudi SMEs' intention to adopt cloud
computing services. Awareness refers to the employees' knowledge of cloud computing
services, benefits, and risks. This research measured this factor using three items
discussed in Chapter 5, Section 5.11.1.16. Therefore, awareness is a very consequential
factor that should be cared about and influences Saudi SMEs' intention to adopt cloud
computing services; as the results of this study revealed a positive correlation between


                                            221
awareness (AW) and intention to adopt cloud services (ITAC) (β = .139, p < 0.043). This
implies that Saudi SMEs feel embracing cloud computing depends on their employees'
awareness. The study results are consistent with those of Hiran (2021), which confirmed
that people's awareness helps accelerate organisations' transition toward cloud adoption.
The results of the current study further indicate that Saudi SMEs' awareness has yet to
reach the level required to push them to adopt cloud services.

The interviews IT managers and top managers confirmed the survey findings. One of the
interviewees (P5) argued that awareness of the Cloud was lacking in SMEs. According
to this top manager in the food sector, this was especially the case for managers, who
were unlikely to have specialist technical knowledge. He believed that generally
knowledge of the Cloud was limited to just knowing that its services were operated
through the Internet and that it was high time that all SME employees were properly
informed about cloud services.

The findings from the survey data and the interview data confirm that Saudi SMEs must
pay greater attention to employee awareness and consider that increasing employee
awareness increases the intention to adopt cloud computing services.

7.1.17 Trust
The quantitative survey results support the hypothesis (H17): Increasing the trust of the
IT managers, top managers and employees increases Saudi SMEs' intention to adopt
cloud computing services. Trust refers to how the workers in SMEs, either regular
employees or IT managers and top managers, believe in and trust cloud computing. This
research measured this factor using three items mentioned in Chapter 5, Section 5.11.1.17.
Therefore, trust is a paramount element that significantly impacts Saudi SMEs' intention
to adopt cloud computing services; and a significant positive relationship between trust
(TU) and Saudi SMEs' intention to adopt cloud services (ITAC), with a critical value (β
= .105, p < 0.005) was found. Previous studies (e.g., Al Mudawi et al., 2022; Jaradat et
al., 2020) agreed that trust is essential to maintain transparency between organisations
and their employees, and encourages them to adopt cloud computing services.

The results of the current study also demonstrate that currently, levels of trust are not
sufficiently high, so SMEs need to enhance their employee's perception of cloud
computing services to raise their trust. The interview findings support this finding. As one


                                            222
of the interviewees (P14) explained, the problem was not a lack of confidence in cloud
computing technology, but rather a lack of trust in cloud providers. According to this top
manager, this mistrust was due to no system of penalties for data leakage being in place,
so SMEs had no recourse to claiming compensation in such cases, and it was this that
delayed the adoption of cloud computing services.

The findings from the perception of other IT managers and top managers agree that trust
is a critical factor in adopting cloud services; and that Saudi SMEs need to consider
increasing their employees' trust in cloud services and improving it to facilitate the
transition to cloud computing services.


    7.2 Summary
In conclusion, this chapter discusses the findings for each factor which were obtained
using two different methods: the primary quantitative method (a survey of Saudi SME
employees) and the auxiliary, complementary qualitative method (semi-structured
interviews with top managers and IT managers). A detailed discussion of the analysis of
the framework's factors that influenced Saudi SMEs' intention to adopt cloud computing
services has been outlined for both samples.

The statistical analysis results were summarised to show whether the hypothesized
relationships between the proposed factors and the Saudi SMEs' intention to adopt cloud
computing services were accepted or rejected. The results from the employee sample
demonstrated that all factors had a positive impact on Saudi SME's intention to adopt
cloud computing services, except Data Security (DS), Service Cost (SC), Organisation
Size (OS), Enterprise Competitiveness (EC) and Culture (CL). IT managers and top
managers, on the other hand, believed that all the factors had a positive impact on the
Saudi SME's intention to adopt cloud computing services, except Data Security (DS),
Organisation Size (OS), and Culture (CL).

The following chapter will answer the research questions and outline the scientific
contributions and recommendations for this research.




                                            223
Chapter
    8 Conclusion and Recommendations
    8.1 Introduction
This chapter concludes the work conducted in this thesis to investigate the factors that
impact Saudi SMEs' adoption of cloud computing services and try to increase and
motivate their intention to adopt cloud services, see Figure 8.1. The research findings will
be summarised and discussed based on the analysis tools used. Then, the research
questions of this study will be discussed and answered by matching findings with each
question. Furthermore, this chapter will describe the methodological contribution made
to the existing knowledge, as well as the findings obtained through the use of many
approaches. In addition, this research will provide recommendations for Saudi SMEs on
adopting cloud computing services, depending on the findings. The study will
demonstrate the research implications and limitations that can enhance the adoption of
cloud computing among Saudi SMEs. Finally, the future work and their intended
expansion will be present.




 Figure 7-2 Stage 8: Validating the Research Model, implications and limitations



                                            224
    8.2 Mapping Research                          Questions,         Findings          and
        Contributions
It was not possible to examine all aspects that could impact Saudi SMEs' adoption of
cloud computing services due to the restricted time and limited available resources.
However, in this thesis, a significant effort has been made to identify the most influential
factors that could affect the cloud adoption process, which led to an investigation into 17
factors. In this context, a literature review, published articles, and papers confirmed that
no study previously had investigated those factors or their aspects regarding SMEs in
developing countries, specifically Saudi Arabia. The findings in the previous chapters,
Chapters 5 and 6, brought to light the novel contribution made to the theoretical
knowledge of cloud computing adoption backed by empirical evidence. In addition, a
constructive contribution to the field has been made by developing a conceptual model
consisting of four main contexts along with all associated factors which are the
Technological context (Data Confidentiality, Data Integrity, Data Security, Relative
Advantages, Service Cost, and Service Quality), the Organisational context (Organisation
Regulations, Organisation Size, Technology Readiness, and Top Management support),
the Environmental context (Technology Infrastructure, Cloud Provider, Legal
Framework, and Enterprise Competitiveness), and the Social context (Culture,
Awareness, and Trust). The current result has contributed to further extending the
knowledge about cloud computing adoption by Saudi SMEs, which enables enterprises
and researchers to assess the process of cloud adoption and its stage.

The main goal of this thesis is to identify and investigate the most influential factors that
impact the adoption of cloud computing services to contribute to and increase the
intention of Saudi SMEs toward adoption. The following research questions have been
developed to achieve that goal.

   1. What is the current situation of the adoption of cloud computing services by
       Saudi Arabia SMEs?

       To answer this question, the importance of cloud computing adoption by SMEs
       and its technical role in accelerating business in Saudi Arabia has been researched
       to identify the benefits of adopting the cloud and the set of motivation factors. In
       addition, a review and exploration of the barriers and challenges to cloud
       computing adoption in the current systems derived from a literature review have


                                            225
   been conducted to identify the hindrances and assess the current situation (see
   Chapter 2).

2. What are the most influential factors that impact the adoption of cloud
   computing services by Saudi SMEs from the perspective of the top managers,
   IT managers, and employees?

   What has been found in the answer to the previous question was utilized to get an
   idea about all the factors that may affect SMEs' adoption of cloud computing in
   general. Then, after assessing the current situation of Saudi SMEs, factors
   affecting SMEs were aligned with local factors that were thought to influence the
   Saudi SMEs. The most influential factors on Saudi SMEs have been identified
   and are being investigated through the survey to answer this question (see Chapter
   3).

3. What is an appropriate conceptual framework for understanding the
   adoption of cloud computing services by SMEs, specifically in Saudi Arabia?

   To answer this question, a review of the existing frameworks and theories has
   been conducted to find the proper framework that can be used to investigate the
   adoption of Cloud computing services by Saudi SMEs. Then, the framework was
   identified with four contexts to examine 17 factors that may impact cloud
   adoption. Based on that, the model of the study was developed to investigate
   influencer factors on Saudi SMEs toward adoption of cloud computing services.
   Finally, statistical analysis was conducted to find the impact factors and revise the
   study model (see Chapter 3 and 5).

4. To what extent is there an impact due to the adoption of cloud computing
   services by Saudi SMEs from the perspective of the IT managers, and top
   managers?

   A series of semi-structured interviews was conducted with top managers and IT
   managers in Saudi SMEs in Riyadh to get their perspectives on adopting cloud
   computing services. This will lead us to answer this question and guide us to either
   support the answer to the previous question or find any contradictions (see
   Chapter 6).


                                        226
The following sections will further discuss how this research answers the above questions
in detail.

8.2.1 Research Question One
The literature review that has been conducted showed that the adoption of cloud
computing services is the key to helping SMEs achieve their progress and lead to their
success in terms of developed and developing countries, including Saudi Arabia.
However, SMEs in Saudi Arabia are still in the early stages of adopting cloud services.
There is a lack of literature that comprehensively investigates the majority of influencer
factors that delay the adoption process of Saudi SMEs. Prior studies mainly examined the
obstacles encountered by SMEs, but their analysis was limited to certain elements and
did not include all influential aspects. Several studies specifically emphasised security
and privacy concerns. Furthermore, most prior studies presented frameworks and models
that emphasised the financial implications of adopting cloud computing services and their
effects on enterprise expenses. However, these studies failed to thoroughly evaluate all
the factors influencing the adoption of cloud computing services. Nevertheless, the
expense, security considerations, and various other factors (such as data confidentiality
and integrity, organisations' regulations, trust, etc) significantly affect the transition from
traditional systems. They can shape the acceptance of cloud computing services.
Therefore, examining only a few factors while disregarding the others fails to provide a
comprehensive understanding, as it is imperative to investigate all the factors involved.
However, as far as the author is aware, no prior study has examined the many aspects that
might influence the adoption of cloud computing services by Saudi SMEs, and most
studies in Saudi Arabia were focused on the public sector. Furthermore, given the nascent
state of cloud computing in Saudi Arabia, the author conducted a comprehensive
investigation into the factors that might influence its adoption. The aim is to develop a
comprehensive framework that can aid Saudi SMEs in making well-informed decisions
regarding adopting cloud computing services.

8.2.2 Research Question Two
The literature conducted for the previous question helped the researcher dive into the
frameworks and theories employed in previous studies to identify the proper one that
helps to study the most influential factors affecting cloud adoption. Then, Chapter 3
examines widely-used research frameworks that can be utilised to investigate the factors


                                             227
of cloud computing service adoption. A survey was undertaken to assess the efficacy of
these frameworks and their underlying factors. The analysis results revealed the most
prevalent research frameworks that can be consistent with this study are the DOI theory
and the TOE framework. However, this study needs to add some factors that do not exist
within this framework and theory. In light of this, this study expands upon the DOI and
TOE framework and establishes the following components as independent variables:

   Ø Technological Context
The technological factor focuses on searching the most influencing factors by studying
the technical aspects that impact an organisation's intent to adopt cloud computing
services. Hence, the following independent six factors (Data Confidentiality, Data
Integrity, Data Security, Relative Advantages, Service Cost, and Service Quality)
examine the most current components that influence the adoption process of cloud
computing services in Saudi SMEs.

   Ø Organisational Context
The organisational factor focuses on searching the most influencing factors by studying
the managerial aspects that impact an organisation's intent to adopt cloud computing
services, explicitly focusing on management and infrastructural issues. The following
four independent factors that come under the organisational factor (Organisation
Regulations, Organisation Size, Technology Readiness, and Top Management support)
focus on scrutinising and discerning business practices based on principles and ideas that
contribute to the rise of the intention of SMEs in Saudi Arabia to adopt cloud services.

   Ø Environmental Context
The environmental factor focuses on searching the most influencing factors by studying
the external environmental aspects that impact an organisation's intent to adopt cloud
computing services. The following four independent factors come under the
environmental factor (Technology Infrastructure, Cloud Provider, Legal Framework, and
Enterprise Competitiveness) and delineate the most significant issues that might hinder
Saudi SMEs' use of cloud computing services.

   Ø Social Context
The social factor focuses on searching for the most influential factors by studying the
people that impact an organisation's intention to adopt cloud computing services. It
encompasses the prevailing attitudes and behaviours of the users. The following three


                                           228
independent factors that come under the social factor (Culture, Awareness, and Trust)
thoroughly examine all the components that impact the inclination of Saudi SMEs to
embrace cloud services, with a focus on the social environment.

Identifying the abovementioned factors that impact upon the adoption of cloud computing
services by Saudi SMEs is essential for organisations aiming to maintain competitiveness
in the current digital environment. By comprehending the complex factors, SMEs may
effectively formulate efficient tactics to tackle any apprehensions or obstacles to adopting
cloud services.

Furthermore, the factors impacting the acceptance of cloud computing services should be
understood early to enable top managers, and IT managers to formulate strategies and
initiatives that promote their adoption. For instance, top managers might actively
encourage investment in infrastructure development, such as acquiring high-speed
internet and enhancing software compatibility, to expedite the adoption of cloud
technology.

8.2.3 Research Question Three
Based on the factors identified in answer to previous questions, this study developed a
comprehensive model called the Adoption of Cloud Computing Model by Saudi SMEs
(ACCM-SME). Prior research on SME adoption of cloud computing was thoroughly
reviewed to produce ACCM-SME, not to mention the many theories and models that have
been applied to determine what elements contribute to the uptake of contemporary
technology. In addition, ACCM-SME incorporates the TOE framework with some of the
critical aspects of DOI theory and some factors that were discovered as a challenge for
SMEs to provide a holistic model that directs this investigation into the aspects
influencing cloud computing adoption. By raising the intention of SMEs in Saudi Arabia
to adopt cloud computing services, the framework contributes to strengthening the image
of cloud computing and examines its effects.

Descriptive and statistical studies were carried out to assess the developed framework. As
a result of these investigations, policymakers will better understand what drives Saudi
SMEs to adopt cloud computing services. The factors of the developed framework
(ACCM-SME) provide the basis for the hypotheses tested in this research. In addition, it




                                            229
helps determine how various factors impact the uptake of cloud services and the
relationship between them.

The results of the SMEs questionnaire were analysed in Chapter 5 to validate the
formulated hypothesis and determine the relationship between independent and
dependent factors regarding adopting cloud computing services. In addition, the results
for each factor of the research model are discussed in section 7.1 in Chapter 7, and the
revised framework is shown in Figure 8.2.




        Figure 7-3 Modified Conceptual Framework Based on the Findings



8.2.4 Research Question Four
In Chapter 6, a theme analysis was performed on the data gathered from the semi-
structured interviews conducted with IT managers and Top managers. The investigation
uncovered intriguing results showcasing their leadership perspectives, significantly
impacting cloud adoption decision-making. These perspectives often showed profound
insights and facilitated a comprehensive understanding of barriers and prospects relevant
to cloud computing adoption by Saudi SMEs.




                                            230
IT and top managers' perspectives on cloud computing adoption may be gleaned via
thematic analysis of interviews. Through this information, researchers and organisations
can understand leaders' challenges while trying to adopt cloud services. By analysing the
interviews, researchers might spot recurring ideas or trends. These recurring ideas might
help current organisations and new startups better comprehend SMEs' difficulties when
intent on adopting cloud computing. Policymakers may use this information to craft their
technology systems and regulations to help the sector expand and thrive. To better
understand SMEs' actual and genuine difficulties while adopting the Cloud, it was helpful
to do a theme analysis of interviews with IT managers and top management. Established
businesses and new ventures may utilise this data to their advantage when planning how
to adopt cloud computing services and stay competitive with peers.

After conducting the thematic analysis in Chapter 6, the researcher found that Seven
themes show the perceptions of participants who engaged in the study, as shown in Figure
8.3, and are discussed in Section 7.1 in Chapter 7 with each factor.

8.3 Methodological Contribution
As described in Chapter 4, this study used a mixed-methods approach to conduct its
research. The aim is to enhance the understanding of the phenomenon by utilising mixed
methods and combining them to uncover their interdependence. Furthermore, the data



                                           231
was collected and analysed using the best research approach to derive the best
conclusions. The mixed approach incorporated the following methods:

   1. Literature Review
       Chapter 2's literature review concentrated on the most recent, pertinent studies on
       SMEs' adoption of cloud computing services. Reviewing previous studies and
       analysing them to assess SMEs' strengths and weaknesses in adopting cloud
       computing services led to identifying their challenges. Then, it guided the
       researcher to develop a comprehensive framework that can assist Saudi SMEs in
       making well-informed decisions regarding cloud computing services, which was
       formed and revised after collecting the main data and analysing them.
   2. Quantitative Method
       The purpose of this method was to examine how employees of SMEs think and
       their beliefs about adopting cloud computing services. A questionnaire has been
       developed specifically for this purpose to gather numerical data. Given the Saudi
       population, achieving a 95% confidence level and a 5% margin of error required
       a sample size of 384. The confidence and margin levels are met, and 412 responses
       were gathered in total. In order to evaluate the hypotheses that were developed,
       the data received from the questionnaire was examined using the Statistical
       Software for the Social Sciences (SPSS) and a descriptive analysis approach.
   3. Qualitative Method
       This method aimed to examine the viewpoints of IT managers and top managers
       on the adoption of cloud computing services by Saudi SMEs. To achieve this
       objective, 15 interviewees representing various sectors of Saudi SMEs in Riyadh
       were interviewed in a semi-structured interview. NVivo software was used to
       analyse the collected data in this research section. Its purpose was to examine the
       gathered data, identify their connections, and construct appropriate themes.

8.4 Cross-Methods Findings
This section is dedicated to comparing the results of the collected data regarding the
intention to adopt cloud computing services from different methods employed in this
research, including the employee questionnaire and interviews with IT managers and top
managers of Saudi SMEs, which are already discussed in the above sections in the




                                          232
answers to questions 3 and 4. This section aims to show the findings and find agreement
and disagreement between them.

level of agreement or disagreement between them. The "AGREE" or "DISAGREE"
comments in each row under each factor signify whether the employees' perspective and
IT managers' and top managers' perspectives agree with the hypothesis or disagree with
it.

There is a disagreement between employees' perspectives and IT managers' and top
managers' perspectives on the cost aspect of cloud service. The disagreement from the
employee side may arise from a lack of information about the expenses associated with
cloud services and the budget of the organisation. However, IT managers and top
managers prioritise the cost of cloud services when considering adopting cloud
computing. This is associated with the well-established finding that one of the advantages
of cloud computing is cost reduction (Vidhyalakshmi & Kumar, 2016).

Another conflict is between employee perspectives and IT managers' and top managers'
perspectives about the enterprise competitiveness factor. Employees believe that
competitiveness does not impact the cloud adoption process by SMEs. On the other hand,
interviews conducted with IT managers and top managers show that the competitiveness
factor catalyses the adoption of cloud computing services. These findings clearly show a
contradiction between employees' views and IT managers' and top managers' views. This
contradiction could be interpreted as a need for employees' awareness of the actual
implementation of competitiveness. In addition, it could mean that competitiveness is not


                                               235
impacting enough from employee viewpoints and that IT managers and top managers are
aware of their implications. The last is most appropriate since it aligns with a study that
found that competitive pressure is an influential factor in adopting the Cloud (Low et al.,
2011).

The table above highlights the possible discrepancy in conclusions obtained from various
analytic methodologies. This contradiction serves as a catalyst for future studies aimed at
offering more clarification and a more comprehensive understanding of the areas of
disagreement and the real interpretation of both employees' questionnaires and interviews
with IT managers and top managers.


8.5 Research Recommendations
This study has produced findings about the factors that impact Saudi SMEs' adoption of
cloud computing services. These findings are beneficial for SMEs that are interested in
adopting innovative technologies, such as cloud computing. This study has developed a
model and then revised it after analysing and collecting data that may assist in making
judgements on adopting cloud computing services into SME systems. The research
provided valuable findings on the primary aspects that impact the adoption of cloud
computing for Saudi SMEs. The following points highlight the recommendations for this
research, based on the findings and knowledge gained, to assist SMEs in successfully
adopting cloud computing services:

   •     Improvement for IT Infrastructure
         This study finds that SMEs need to look after their infrastructure, including
         internet services and systems compatibility, to make their process for adoption of
         cloud services easier. It noticed that most participants were worried about their
         internet speed and bandwidth as some SMEs still use cable internet services
         instead of fibre-optic internet. In addition, most Saudi SMEs still need help with
         their systems, which are incompatible with cloud service providers. Adopting any
         new system should be reviewed before based on the cloud provider's requirement
         to make sure it is compatible and can be transferred to cloud provider servers.
         These recommendations would enhance the process of adopting cloud computing
         services. Moreover, IT leaders and top managers should care about these by taking
         immediate action plans to fix the mentioned issues. They should use the



                                            236
    advantages of existing services to accelerate Saudi SMEs' adoption of cloud
    services to align with the vision of Saudi Arabia 2030, which focuses on
    improving the quality of technologies and services provided for organisations and
    individuals.
•   Improvement in Data Confidentiality and Integrity
    The study's findings indicate that SMEs are worried about data confidentiality and
    integrity when adopting cloud computing services. This issue arises from the
    possibility that certain cloud providers may share the private customer data of
    SMEs in exchange for marketing objectives. The recommendation for this issue
    is that it can be resolved from the government side by taking immediate action to
    implement efficient data regulations to safeguard the data of SMEs. Furthermore,
    it is imperative to thoroughly evaluate and enforce stringent regulations and
    standards regarding data to prevent any unauthorised transfer or data exchange by
    cloud providers.
•   Improvement in the Number of Cloud Providers within Saudi
    The development of cloud technology in Saudi Arabia is now in its early stages.
    Collaboration between the private sector and the government is recommended to
    increase the number of cloud service providers in Saudi Arabia. In recent years,
    the Saudi government implemented legislation mandating that any organisation
    handling the data of citizens and residents must store and process it using cloud
    providers whose servers are located within the Saudi border since the local
    provider numbers are still modest. The Saudi Vision 2030 aims to enhance the
    number of cloud providers by devising suitable regulations and strategies for the
    growth of domestic cloud services, and this is what reinforces this
    recommendation. Moreover, the findings of this study are valuable in garnering
    support for cloud computing adoption by Saudi SMEs.
•   Improvement in the Trust and Awareness of Cloud Services
    The study's findings revealed that trust and awareness are essential to adopting
    cloud computing services. As the interviewees stated, these factors are subject to
    the level of education and training of people working within SMEs regarding
    cloud adoption. Therefore, the recommendation for this issue is that SMEs should
    regularly organise workshops and training sessions for their employees, from top




                                       237
       management to standard employees, to make them aware of cloud services, which
       directly reflects their trust in cloud services and leads to their adoption.


8.6 Research Implications
Due to the improvements that cloud computing has made in the field of technology and
the advantage the cloud gives, it has become trendy and desired by many organisations.
This study has investigated empirically to understand the challenges and obstacles that
hinder organisations from adopting cloud services from different perspectives and
contexts. This study has a considerable sample size as it collected 412 responses for the
quantitative method (survey) and 15 interviews for the qualitative method (semi-
structured interviews). The findings of this study may contribute to assisting organisations
and their leadership to understand the accurate perceptions of those organisations, such
as technical aspects. In addition, it may help organisations reformulate their rules and
strategies which is consistent with factors that this study has proved as challenges which
SMEs face. The findings can be generalised to all private sectors around all cities of Saudi
Arabia as the sample was collected from the more prominent and more influential city,
Riyadh. In addition, they could be applied to Gulf countries as they share the same culture,
infrastructure, and business practices.

The researchers highlight that by drawing from many theoretical frameworks, they were
able to examine SMEs' use of cloud computing from a more comprehensive vantage
point. For this reason, the empirical study was designed around identifying and assessing
the most critical aspects and challenges to create a thorough research framework. Then,
this research after a deep investigation in the literature, resulted in the framework
(ACCM-SME) based on the merging of two established theories called the TOE model
and DOI theory, which may give helpful insights for businesses. The research also
clarified and highlighted the importance of leaders in fostering an environment conducive
to developing systems that need the involvement of organisational leaders with the skills
to overcome obstacles in adopting and implementing suitable information technology.
Several factors that might encourage and reinforce businesses to switch to cloud-based
systems have been explored in this research.

In conclusion, this research examined four contexts—the technological context, the
organisational context, the environmental context, and the social context—to test all


                                            238
associated problem elements. It looked at the whole picture to determine why SMEs are
not yet moving to the Cloud. There were crucial findings for SMEs, particularly in Saudi
Arabia which may increase their intention to adopt cloud computing. As such, the
developed conceptual framework will serve as a good jumping-off point for SMEs when
they intend to start adopting cloud services


8.7 Research Limitations and Future Study Directions
This study's results indicate how SMEs in future can both benefit from and adopt cloud
computing. Nonetheless, various limitations have been highlighted, giving an opportunity
to investigate them. Top managers, IT managers, and employees of SMEs were among
the survey respondents for this research. As a result, there are two limitations that were
outside of the study scope. First, the study has not considered the views of consumers or
cloud computing service providers. Secondly, it does not consider the potential job-cut
opportunities that may arise from the SME's adoption of cloud computing, and which may
influence their choice to adopt it. These limitations may be overcome in the future as new
variables are studied.

The intention of SMEs to adopt cloud computing services is found to be a critical matter
in the context of technological, environmental, organisational, and social factors, which
necessitates additional investigation. Thus, this study investigated this phenomenon as an
initial step in exploring cloud computing adoption among SMEs. Therefore, emphasising
the limitations mentioned in the above has brought to light an exciting area that presents
prospects for future investigations, which is highlighted in the following points:

   •   The limitations that have been mentioned necessitate additional research to
       thoroughly examine certain factors that were out of the study scope, including the
       cloud providers' perspective, the customers' perspective, and the potential job loss
       factors. Future research on these factors would contribute to understanding their
       influence and add knowledge to the current findings. Exploring the whole picture
       of factors affecting SMEs' intention to adopt cloud computing services from
       different angles is very beneficial. It should be noted that the framework
       developed in this thesis is receptive to further factors that can be explored.
   •   This study used a semi-structured interview method with IT managers and top
       managers to examine their perspectives on SMEs' adoption of cloud computing



                                           239
    services. Then, it utilised a thematic analysis approach to find the proper themes
    in their collected responses. This approach efficiently gathers open-ended data
    and has proven valuable in uncovering intriguing discoveries not found in
    employee survey responses. However, due to limited number of samples the
    conclusions are not exhaustive. This opens an opportunity for future research to
    develop a study that gathers data from many IT managers and top managers using
    two questionnaires (quantitative), each of which focuses on a single type of
    sample. This could help to reinforce the current findings of this study.
•   This study investigated the challenges that SMEs face in the adoption of cloud
    computing services in the context of Saudi Arabia. However, the conclusions of
    this study could potentially be relevant to MENA, specifically the Gulf
    Cooperation Council countries, as their market practices and cultures are similar
    (Alsharari et al., 2020; Awad, 2020). Furthermore, this opens a chance for this
    study and future studies to use this direction and explore if this study's revised
    model for cloud computing adoption by SMEs applies to other neighbouring
    countries.
•   This study presented and validated the theoretical framework for adopting cloud
    computing services. Based on the factors investigated, it will be used to develop
    cloud-based software. This software encompasses all the requirements of SMEs
    in a single cloud-based solution.




                                        240
8.8 Conclusion
This study has investigated the intention of Saudi SMEs to adopt cloud computing
services, focusing on technological, environmental, organizational, and social factors.
The Adoption of the Cloud Computing Model by Saudi SMEs (ACCM-SME) framework
was developed and validated through a mixed-method approach involving both
quantitative and qualitative data. The findings reveal that cloud computing adoption in
Saudi Arabia is still in its early stages, but a growing trend toward broader adoption is
evident. Key factors influencing adoption were identified, with 12 out of 17 accepted
hypotheses. The statistical analysis results were summarized to show whether the
hypothesized relationships between the proposed factors and the Saudi SMEs' intention
to adopt cloud computing services were accepted or rejected. The results from the
employee sample demonstrated that all factors had a positive impact on Saudi SMEs'
intention to adopt cloud computing services, except Data Security (DS), Service Cost
(SC), Organization Size (OS), Enterprise Competitiveness (EC), and Culture (CL). IT
managers and top managers, on the other hand, believed that all the factors had a positive
impact on Saudi SMEs' intention to adopt cloud computing services, except Data Security
(DS), Organization Size (OS), and Culture (CL). These insights underscore the factors
driving cloud adoption, which can help cloud providers enhance their services and assist
policymakers and business leaders in formulating strategies that facilitate cloud adoption
among Saudi SMEs.
Despite the valuable insights gained, several limitations of this study were identified,
creating opportunities for further research. The perspectives of consumers and cloud
computing service providers were not considered, nor were the potential implications of
job loss due to cloud adoption. Future research will provide a more comprehensive
understanding of the factors influencing cloud adoption. Additionally, the study used
semi-structured interviews with IT and top managers as a thematic analysis approach,
allowing for open-ended exploration of their perspectives. However, the sample size was
limited to Riyadh city, highlighting the need for future research with larger, more diverse
samples from different cities to reinforce these findings.

Moreover, the study's conclusions have potential relevance beyond Saudi Arabia,
particularly for the Gulf Cooperation Council countries, due to similarities in market
practices and cultures. Future studies could explore whether the revised model for cloud
computing adoption by SMEs can be applied to other neighbouring countries. Lastly, the


                                            241
theoretical framework developed in this study could serve as the basis for creating a
comprehensive cloud-based solution for SMEs, encompassing all their requirements in a
single software package.

In summary, this study significantly contributes to the knowledge of cloud computing
adoption among Saudi SMEs, providing a foundation for further research and practical
implications for cloud service providers, policymakers, and business leaders.

Please note and follow the requirements for approved submissions:

Amendments to protocol
    * Any changes or amendments to approved protocols must be submitted to the C-REC for authorisation prior to implementation.
Feedback regarding the status and conduct of approved projects
    * Any incidents with ethical implications that occur during the implementation of the project must be reported immediately to the
       Chair of the C-REC.
Feedback regarding any adverse(1) and unexpected events(2)
    * Any adverse (undesirable and unintended) and unexpected events that occur during the implementation of the project must be
       reported to the Chair of the Science and Technology C-REC. In the event of a serious adverse event, research must be stopped
       immediately and the Chair alerted within 24 hours of the occurrence.

Monitoring of Approved studies
The University may undertake periodic monitoring of approved studies. Researchers will be requested to report on the outcomes of
research activity in relation to approvals that were granted (full applications and amendments).

Research Standards
Failure to conduct University research in alignment with the Code of Practice for Research may be investigated under the Procedure
for the Investigation of Allegations of Misconduct in Research or other appropriate internal mechanisms (3). Any queries can be
addressed to the Research Governance Office: rgoffice@sussex.ac.uk

(1) An "adverse event" is one that occurs during the course of a research protocol that either causes physical or psychological harm,
or increases the risk of physical or psychological harm, or results in a loss of privacy and/or confidentiality to research participant or
others.

(2) An "unexpected event" is an occurrence or situation during the course of a research project that was a) harmful to a participant
taking part in the research, or b) increased the probability of harm to participants taking part in the research.

(3) http://www.sussex.ac.uk/staff/research/rqi/policy/research-policy

Appendix C: Information sheet for Questionnaire




                              INFORMATION SHEET FOR THE SURVEY

   Dear Participant,

   Thank you for your participation in this study. I am Mohammed Alqahtani a PhD student at
   the University of Sussex, Informatics Department, United Kingdom. This questionnaire is part of
   my research as partial fulfilment of a Doctor of Philosophy (PhD) at the University of Sussex. The
   title of the research is “A New Adoption of Cloud Computing Model for Saudi Arabian SMEs
   (ACCM-SME) to investigate the Barriers, Challenges and Success Factors. The research aims to
   identify, investigate, and discuss the most significant challenges that face Cloud computing within
   SMEs in Saudi Arabia that play a significant impact on the SMEs intention toward adoption of
   Cloud computing services. This research will contribute to a better understanding of the analysing
   of barriers and challenges factors to improve the adoption of Cloud services.
   By participating in the study, you will help the researchers to gain a clear picture of the challenges
   that affects SMEs intention. The survey will take about 15 minutes to complete. The questionnaire
   consists of questions divided into 2 sections. The first 11 questions (first section) contain general
   demographic information about the participants. The second section contains the main study
   questions.
   Your participation in the survey is entirely voluntary. The survey is entirely anonymous, and at no
   point in the survey will you be asked for any information that will be able to identify you. None of
   the information you provide will be able to be used to trace you. You are free to withdraw from the
   survey at any time, even after you begin the survey, with no explanation required. The information
   you provide in the survey will only be used for academic purposes and will be entirely limited to
   the scope of this study. No third parties are involved in this study, and your information will not be
   shared with any third parties. All collected data will be stored in a de- identified way (e.g. using ID
   numbers not names), and kept separate from other details about participants (e.g. from the
   consent form). Electronic data will be stored in a password-protected file on a University of Sussex
   Cloud-based server. The results of analysing the data will only be used for research purposes. If
   you would like to receive a copy of the results, please contact me at my email address.
   Your participation in the study is greatly appreciated and will have a great contribution to this
   research.
   The University of Sussex has insurance in place to cover its legal liabilities concerning this study.
   This study has been approved by the Sciences & Technology Cross-Schools Research Ethics
   Committee (crecscitec@sussex.ac.uk). The project reference number is (ER/MA2251/1). If you
   like to withdraw your data from this research, you will need to email your request to the researcher
   at ma2251@sussex.ac.uk. The deadline for such withdrawal will be 2 weeks after the data
   collection date.

   For further information or in case of any queries during completing the questionnaire, you can
   contact me at:
   Email: ma2251@sussex.ac.uk
   If you have any concerns about the way in which the study has been conducted, please contact
   my supervisor and the ethics committee (C-REC):
   Dr. Natalia Beloff: N.Beloff@sussex.ac.uk
   Department of Informatics, University of Sussex, Falmer, Brighton BN1 9QJ
   Ethics Committee (C-REC): crecscitec@sussex.ac.uk


   Thank you for your participation. Mohammed Alqahtani

Appendix F: Information Sheet for Interview




                              INFORMATION SHEET FOR INTERVIEW

  Dear Participant,

  Thank you for your participation in this study. I am Mohammed Alqahtani a PhD student at
  the University of Sussex, Informatics Department, United Kingdom. This interview is part of my
  research as partial fulfilment of a Doctor of Philosophy (PhD) at the University of Sussex. The title
  of the research is “A New Adoption of Cloud Computing Model for Saudi Arabian SMEs (ACCM-
  SME) to investigate the Barriers, Challenges and Success Factors. The research aims to identify,
  investigate, and discuss the most significant challenges that face Cloud computing within SMEs
  in Saudi Arabia that play a significant impact on the SMEs intention toward adoption of Cloud
  computing services. This research will contribute to a better understanding of the analysing of
  barriers and challenges factors to improve the adoption of Cloud services.
  By participating in the study, you will help the researcher to gain a clear picture of the challenges
  that affects SMEs intention. The interview will take about 15 minutes to complete. The interview
  consists of 12 items.
  Your participation in the interview is entirely voluntary. The interview is entirely anonymous, and
  at no point in the interview will you be asked for any information that will be able to identify you.
  None of the information you provide will be able to be used to trace you. You are free to withdraw
  from the interview at any time, even after you begin the interview, with no explanation required.
  The information you provide in the interview will only be used for academic purposes and will be
  entirely limited to the scope of this study. No third parties are involved in this study, and your
  information will not be shared with any third parties. All collected data will be stored in a de-
  identified way (e.g. using ID numbers not names), and kept separate from other details about
  participants (e.g. from the consent form). Electronic data will be stored in a password-protected
  file on a University of Sussex Cloud-based server. The results of analysing the data will only be
  used for research purposes. If you would like to receive a copy of the results, please contact me
  at my email address.
  Your participation in the study is greatly appreciated and will have a great contribution to this
  research. The location of the interviews will be based on your preference in any place in Riyadh
  city. However, if you prefer to do the interview online, then it will be held through the Sussex
  University Teams or Zoom account.
  The University of Sussex has insurance in place to cover its legal liabilities concerning this study.
  This study has been approved by the Sciences & Technology Cross-Schools Research Ethics
  Committee (crecscitec@sussex.ac.uk). The project reference number is (ER/MA2251/1). A
  unique identifier will be given to each participant. The participants will be advised to retain their
  identifiers in case they want to withdraw their data from this research in the future. If they decided
  to proceed with the withdrawal of their data, they will need to email the researcher at
  ma2251@sussex.ac.uk. with the unique identifier and request the removal of their data before
  the deadline without needing to give any reason or explanation. The deadline for such withdrawal
  is set for two weeks after completion of the interview.

  For further information or in case of any queries during completing the interview, you can contact
  me at: Email: ma2251@sussex.ac.uk
  If you have any concerns about the way in which the study has been conducted, please contact
  my supervisor and the ethics committee (C-REC):
  Dr. Natalia Beloff: N.Beloff@sussex.ac.uk
  Department of Informatics, University of Sussex, Falmer, Brighton BN1 9QJ
  Ethics Committee (C-REC): crecscitec@sussex.ac.uk

  Thank you for your participation. Mohammed Alqahtani

Appendix H: Interview Questions




  Interview Guide from a managerial perspective at Saudi SMEs with the top
  managers and IT managers.


  Q1\ Have you adopted cloud computing services in your organisation?
  Why?
  Q2\ Could you please tell me about the obstacles and challenges that your organisation has
  encountered in using cloud computing services based on your experience?
  Q3\ How well do you feel your organisation is aware of cloud computing?
  Q4\ If there are any obstacles that prevent you from adopting cloud computing could you
  please tell me about them?
  Q5\ Based on your experience, what are the factors that pose hurdles to cloud computing
  adoption?
  Q6\ What advantages do you believe the cloud computing may provide to an organisation?
  Q7\ What technological factors do you think may impact the adoption of cloud computing in
  your organisation? (e.g., data confidentiality, data integrity, data security, relative advantages,
  service cost, and service quality) why?
  Q8\ What organisational factors do you think may impact the adoption of cloud computing in
  your organisation? (e.g., organisation regulations, organisation size, technology readiness, and
  top management support) why?
  Q9\ What environmental factors do you think may impact the adoption of cloud computing in
  your organisation? (e.g., technology infrastructure, Cloud provider, legal framework, and
  enterprise competitiveness) why?
  Q10\ What Social factors do you think may impact the adoption of cloud computing in your
  organisation? (e.g., culture, awareness, and trust) why?
  Q11\ Do you intend to use cloud computing in the future?
  Q12\ Do you want to add anything about the adoption of cloud computing by SMEs in Saudi
  Arabia?




                                                             288
